<p>In the <b><a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> elections in 1828</b>, the Jacksonians soundly took control of the presidency, with <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a>'s victory, and greatly increased their majority in Congress. Outgoing President <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>'s unpopularity played a major role in the Jacksonian pick-up, as did the perception of the Anti-Jacksonian Party as urban and elitist. Major increases in suffrage also heightened Jacksonian wins, as newly enfranchised voters tended to associate with Jacksonian principles. The Anti-Masonic Party, a single issue faction based on distrust of <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Freemasonry</a>, became the first third party in American history to garner seats in the House.</p>
<p></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Peleg_Sprague_(Maine_politician)" title="Peleg Sprague (Maine politician)">Peleg Sprague</a> (AJ) of the <a href="/wiki/Maine%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="Maine's 4th congressional district">4th district</a> resigned upon being elected to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a> and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maine%27s_4th_congressional_district_special_election,_1829&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maine's 4th congressional district special election, 1829 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/George_Evans_(American_politician)" title="George Evans (American politician)">George Evans</a> (AJ)</p>
<p>The election in the <a href="/wiki/Maine%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Maine's 6th congressional district">6th district</a> was not resolved until near the end of the 1st session.</p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Hector_Craig" title="Hector Craig">Hector Craig</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="New York's 6th congressional district">6th district</a> resigned July 12, 1830 and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=New_York%27s_6th_congressional_district_special_election,_1830&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="New York's 6th congressional district special election, 1830 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_W._Eager" title="Samuel W. Eager">Samuel W. Eager</a> (AJ)</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="New York's 20th congressional district">20th district</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silas_Wright" title="Silas Wright">Silas Wright, Jr.</a> (J) successfully contested the election of <a href="/wiki/George_Fisher_(New_York)" title="George Fisher (New York)">George Fisher</a> (AJ); but Wright never claimed the seat, and resigned, without serving, on March 9, 1830. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=New_York%27s_20th_congressional_district_special_election,_1830&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="New York's 20th congressional district special election, 1830 (page does not exist)">A special election</a> was held in November 1830, which was won with 60.6% of the vote by <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Sanford" title="Jonah Sanford">Jonah Sanford</a> (J) over Harvey D. Smith (NR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY-20_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NY-20-13">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Monell" title="Robert Monell">Robert Monell</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_21st_congressional_district" title="New York's 21st congressional district">21st district</a> resigned February 21, 1831</p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Samuel_D._Ingham" title="Samuel D. Ingham">Samuel D. Ingham</a> (J) and <a href="/wiki/George_Wolf" title="George Wolf">George Wolf</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania's 8th congressional district">8th district</a> resigned in March, 1829 and August 31, 1829, respectively. Both were replaced in <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_8th_congressional_district_special_election,_1829" title="Pennsylvania's 8th congressional district special election, 1829">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ihrie,_Jr." title="Peter Ihrie, Jr.">Peter Ihrie, Jr.</a> (J) and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_A._Smith" title="Samuel A. Smith">Samuel A. Smith</a> (J).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_Wilkins_(U.S._politician)" title="William Wilkins (U.S. politician)">William Wilkins</a> (AM) of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_16th_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania's 16th congressional district">16th district</a> resigned November 9, 1829 and was replaced in <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_16th_congressional_district_special_election,_1829" title="Pennsylvania's 16th congressional district special election, 1829">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Harmar_Denny" title="Harmar Denny">Harmar Denny</a> (AM).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vermont"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Vermont" title="List of United States Representatives from Vermont">Vermont</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1828&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Vermont">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vermont electoral law required a majority for election. Two elections were required in the <a href="/wiki/Vermont%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Vermont's 3rd congressional district">3rd district</a> and 8 in the <a href="/wiki/Vermont%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="Vermont's 5th congressional district">5th district</a> to achieve a majority. Only the first and final elections are shown here.</p>

<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Virginia%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Virginia's 1st congressional district">1st district</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Loyall" title="George Loyall">George Loyall</a> (J) successfully contested the election of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Newton,_Jr." title="Thomas Newton, Jr.">Thomas Newton, Jr.</a> (AJ) and was seated March 9, 1830 during the 1st session.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_C._Rives" title="William C. Rives">William C. Rives</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia%27s_10th_congressional_district" title="Virginia's 10th congressional district">10th district</a> resigned before Congress met and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia%27s_10th_congressional_district_special_election,_1829&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Virginia's 10th congressional district special election, 1829 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/William_F._Gordon" title="William F. Gordon">William F. Gordon</a> (J)</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_Pendelton_Barbour" title="Philip Pendelton Barbour">Philip P. Barbour</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia%27s_11th_congressional_district" title="Virginia's 11th congressional district">11th district</a> resigned October 15, 1830 to accept President Jackson's appointment to be judge of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Eastern_District_of_Virginia" title="United States District Court for the Eastern District of Virginia">United States District Court for the Eastern District of Virginia</a> and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia%27s_11th_congressional_district_special_election,_1830&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Virginia's 11th congressional district special election, 1830 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_M._Patton" title="John M. Patton">John M. Patton</a> (J)</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Smyth" title="Alexander Smyth">Alexander Smyth</a> (J) of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia%27s_22nd_congressional_district" title="Virginia's 22nd congressional district">22nd district</a> died April 17, 1830 and was replaced in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Virginia%27s_22nd_congressional_district_special_election,_1830&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Virginia's 22nd congressional district special election, 1830 (page does not exist)">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Draper" title="Joseph Draper">Joseph Draper</a> (J)</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1828&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
